2026-05-06 | round37 Serre modularity core | Ripple: proved the local SL₂ derivative anomaly and Serre cancellation needed for the E4 Ramanujan route. Added denominator derivative helpers, `det_map_SL_complex`, public `normalizedDeriv_slash_action_SL`, `serreDerivative_slash_action_SL`, `serreDerivative_slash_invariant_SL`, Cauchy-estimate infrastructure `normalizedDeriv_isBoundedAtImInfty_of_bounded`, and `E2_eq_one_sub_sigma_qExpansion`. `lake build Ripple.Number.Modular.ModularPolynomialQExpansion`, `ModularPolynomialSturmCertificate`, and `CMEvaluation163` pass; active modular audit remains the same three named sorrys.
2026-05-06 | round37 CRT manifest verifier | Ripple: added `--verify-crt-json` to `scripts/check_phi41_sturm_recurrence.py`. The verifier reloads a manifest, recomputes all listed prime residues/valuations/hash values, rechecks exact or log bound sections when present, and exits nonzero on mismatch. Added `--lean-crt-skeleton`, which turns a manifest into a standalone Lean namespace block applying `phi41Level41RecurrenceCoeffArrayFirstZero_of_prime_crt_bounded_certificate` with explicit prime-list data and remaining `hbound`/`hB`/`hmods` assumptions. Positive smoke test: generate `--bound 20 --extra 0 --primes 1000003 --crt-json --crt-json-exact-bound` then verify it, yielding `ok=true`; generated Lean skeleton compiles. Negative smoke test: mutate the stored valuation to `19`, and verifier returns `ok=false` with the expected valuation mismatch.
2026-05-06 | round37 CRT manifest generator | Ripple: extended `scripts/check_phi41_sturm_recurrence.py` with `--crt-json`, `--crt-json-exact-bound`, and `--crt-json-log-bound`. The manifest records bound/precision, prime product size, distinct/primality checks for the listed 64-bit primes, each prime's valuation and Sturm-zero result, SHA-256 hashes of Sturm-range residues, and optional exact or log coefficient-bound sizing. Added `--lean-prime-list`, which emits Lean definitions plus `Nodup` and `Nat.Prime` proofs for the selected primes. Added `--auto-prime-count` / `--auto-prime-bits` to choose descending primes automatically. Verified small runs: `--bound 80 --extra 0 --primes 1000003,1000033 --crt-json --crt-json-exact-bound` reports `all_sturm_zero=true`, exact bound needs 438 product bits, and the two-prime product is correctly marked too small; `--bound 80 --extra 0 --auto-prime-count 22 --auto-prime-bits 20 --crt-json --crt-json-exact-bound` gives 440 product bits and `product_gt_max_bound=true`; legacy `--primes` output still works; the generated two-prime Lean snippet compiles against `ModularPolynomialSturmCertificate`.
2026-05-06 | round37 CRT proof interface | Ripple: added Lean-side CRT certificate lemmas for the recurrence first-zero route. New facts include `int_eq_zero_of_modEq_zero_of_abs_lt`, list-product CRT merging for pairwise coprime natural moduli, `list_pairwise_coprime_of_nodup_prime`, `int_eq_zero_of_modEq_zero_list_of_abs_lt_prod`, bounded variants accepting `|coeff| ≤ B < product`, and generic `truncCoeffListFirstZero_of_crt_certificate` / `truncCoeffArrayFirstZero_of_crt_certificate` exits, plus the specialized `phi41Level41RecurrenceCoeffArrayFirstZero_of_crt_certificate`, bounded variant, and prime-list variant. These turn per-prime modular zero checks plus a product-size absolute coefficient bound into the Bool first-zero shape used by the Φ₄₁ Sturm certificate. `lake build Ripple.Number.Modular.ModularPolynomialSturmCertificate` passes; active modular audit remains three named `sorry`s.
2026-05-06 06:47 | round37 recovery | Ripple: added recurrence-to-certificate bridge lemmas for the Φ₄₁ finite coefficient route. Proved row-array stability and specialization theorems: once a recurrence coefficient is pushed, later row extension does not change it; final recurrence rows have zero coefficients below valuation `42-j`, leading coefficient `1`, and the expected recurrence above valuation. Added `ListArrayEq.of_phi41QRecurrence`, an abstract uniqueness bridge showing any list row with the same initial conditions and recurrence equals the recurrence array. Added `phi41LevelOneDenseRowsList`, generic evaluator bridge `ListArrayEq.evalSparseCompressedMatrixFromProductTables`, table bridge `ListArrayTableEq.phi41LevelOneDenseRows_of_recurrence`, and `ListArrayEq.phi41Level41CoeffCompressedMatrix_of_recurrenceRows`. This reduces the finite-certificate connection problem to proving each dense row `E4^(3j) * Delta^(42-j)` satisfies the Ramanujan recurrence in the existing truncated-list model. `lake build Ripple.Number.Modular.ModularPolynomialSturmCertificate` passes.

2026-05-06 06:03 | round37 recovery | Ripple: added and reverified `scripts/check_phi41_sturm_recurrence.py`, a recurrence-based Φ₄₁ Sturm coefficient checker using `E4 * q dQ_j/dq = (42 E2 E4 - j E6) * Q_j` for `Q_j = E4^(3j) Delta^(42-j)`. Full mod-prime run `--bound 3528 --extra 0 --prime 1000003` returns `VALUATION 3528` and `STURM_ZERO 1`, avoiding the dense 43×43 level-one power-table bottleneck that killed the PARI/GP route. 2026-05-06 | round37 coefficient bounds | Ripple: added `--bound-bits` and `--bound-log-bits` to the recurrence checker to estimate triangle-inequality coefficient bounds for CRT sizing. Exact bounds report 438 required product bits at `N=80` and 4087 bits at `N=500`; exact full `N=3528` was interrupted after about 4 minutes. The log-bound estimator agrees with the exact small runs up to the configured 8-bit safety margin and finishes at the Sturm bound: `--bound 3528 --extra 0 --bound-log-bits` reports max index 3527, max log bound 28532 bits, so CRT product bits needed are 28533. With nominal 61-bit primes, that is 468 primes under this crude bound.

2026-05-06 | round37 S6 brick | Ripple: proved a private `dim_S6_level_one_zero` in `CMEvaluation163.lean` by the same divide-by-Δ argument as the existing `dim_S4_level_one_zero`: for `f : CuspForm Γ(1) 6`, `f^2/Δ` is weight 0, bounded at cusps, tends to 0 at infinity, hence is the zero constant. `lake build Ripple.Number.Modular.CMEvaluation163` passes.
2026-05-06 | round37 M6 bridge | Ripple: moved the first reusable weight-6 level-one infrastructure into `ModularPolynomialQExpansion.lean`, where the Sturm certificate can import it without a cycle. This sets up the reduction of `M_6(Γ(1))` to the already proved private `S_6(Γ(1)) = 0` brick, which still needs to be lifted into the import path. `lake build Ripple.Number.Modular.ModularPolynomialQExpansion` and `lake build Ripple.Number.Modular.ModularPolynomialSturmCertificate` pass, with only the existing three active modular sorrys.
2026-05-06 | round37 M6 dimension | Ripple: lifted the divide-by-`Delta` weight-6 cusp vanishing argument into `ModularPolynomialQExpansion.lean` as reusable theorem `levelOne_cuspForm_weight6_eq_zero`. Combined it with the q-expansion constant-term bridge to prove `levelOne_weight6_eq_valueAtInfty_smul_E6`, i.e. every `ModularForm Γ(1) 6` is its value at infinity times `E6`. `lake build Ripple.Number.Modular.ModularPolynomialQExpansion` passes. This closes the level-one dimension input for the E4 Ramanujan route; the remaining work for `sigma_convolution_E4_Ramanujan` is Serre-derivative modularity / q-expansion coefficient extraction.
2026-05-06 | round37 Serre infrastructure | Ripple: added more reusable level-one modular-form infrastructure in `ModularPolynomialQExpansion.lean`: `levelOne_modularForm_tendsto_valueAtInfty`, public `E4_tendsto_one_atImInfty` / `E6_tendsto_one_atImInfty`, and `levelOne_isBoundedAt_of_slash_invariant_of_boundedAtInfty`, which lets a slash-invariant level-one candidate get all cusp boundedness from boundedness at infinity.
